Montoy v. State


No. 88,440


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


275 Kan. 145; 62 P.3d 228; 2003 Kan. LEXIS 16



January 24, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Montoy v. State, 278 Kan. 765, 102 P.3d 1158, 2005 Kan. LEXIS 1 (2005)
Subsequent appeal at Montoy v. State, 278 Kan. 769, 102 P.3d 1160, 2005 Kan. LEXIS 2 (2005)
Later proceeding at Montoy v. State, 2005 Kan. LEXIS 460 (Kan., Jan. 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court, TERRY L. BULLOCK, judge.



DISPOSITION: District court judgment reversed, and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a constitutional challenge to the state scheme of financing public education, plaintiffs, numerous students and two school districts, sued defendants, the State, the governor, the chairperson of the Kansas State Board of Education, and the Commissioner of the Kansas State Department of Education. The Shawnee District Court, Kansas, sua sponte granted judgment to defendants. The students and the school districts appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the students and the school districts contended the trial court erred by excluding certain claims on the grounds that they were outside the pleadings, by failing to treat the dismissal of their case as a dismissal based upon a motion for summary judgment, and by concluding that they failed to present legally sufficient claims. The supreme court found the three issues of capital outlay, special education excess costs, and encroachment on the general supervision responsibility of the board were sufficiently raised and should have been considered by the trial court in its resolution of this case. Further, the trial court's judgment failed to address the factual allegations of the students and the school districts; thus, the supreme court concluded that there remained genuine issues of material fact not shown to be a sham, frivolous, or so unsubstantial that it would be futile to try the case. The issues raised in the case required the trial court to determine either on the basis of uncontroverted facts or on facts determined by trial whether the school financing provisions complained of were constitutional.

Mudd v. Neosho Mem. Reg'l Med. Ctr.


No. 89,091


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


275 Kan. 187; 62 P.3d 236; 2003 Kan. LEXIS 23



January 24, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Workers Compensation Board.



DISPOSITION: Workers Compensation Board decision reversed; claim for benefits denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimants, surviving spouse and dependant children, sought survivor benefits under the Workers' Compensation Act, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-501 et seq., from respondent employer and its insurer. An administrative law judge (ALJ) denied the claim. Claimants appealed, and the Kansas Workers Compensation Board reversed the ALJ and awarded benefits to claimants. The employer and its insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a nurse at a regional medical center who died after suffering a rupture of a cerebral aneurysm (stroke) at work. The employee worked in the intensive care unit and the emergency room, and she was required to help resuscitate dying patients. The expert testimony showed that running to respond to "code blues," combined with the stress of code blue situations, probably combined to cause the employee's stroke. The Kansas Supreme Court held that: (1) there was not substantial competent evidence to support the board's finding of unusual exertion under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-501(e), as the employee was required to run in response to a code blue at least once a month as a part of her job duties; (2) stress did not qualify as an "external factor," which would have made Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-501(e) irrelevant to the claim; and (3) Kan. Stat. Ann. § 44-501(e) did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of the U.S. Constitution, as the statute's purpose implicated a legitimate goal, and the means chosen by the legislature bore a rational relationship to that goal.


OUTCOME: The decision of the workers' compensation board was reversed, and the decision of the administrative law judge denying the claim for benefits was affirmed.

 

360 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cullen


No. 87,853


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


275 Kan. 56; 60 P.3d 933; 2003 Kan. LEXIS 2



January 10, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at In re Cullen, 2004 Kan. Unpub. LEXIS 44 (Kan., Dec. 17, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Johnson district court; THOMAS H. BORNHOLDT, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Johnson District Court, Kansas, convicted defendant of attempted rape and gave defendant an upward durational departure sentence and an extended post-release supervision term. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his upward durational sentence imposed under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4716 (Supp. 2001) was unconstitutional, even though defendant, in a plea agreement, recommended that the trial court impose an upward durational departure sentence; and defendant's extended post-release supervision period was unconstitutional. The appellate court had jurisdiction to correct illegal sentences at any time. An upward durational departure sentence imposed under § 21-4716 was clearly vulnerable to constitutional attack, and the merits of that attack would be considered. The Kansas scheme for upward durational departure sentences was unconstitutional on its face. No authority provided by the State suggested that a defendant could submit by waiver to the application of an unconstitutional sentencing scheme. Defendant's upward departure sentence, even though a product of defendant's agreement with the State, was void and could not stand. Defendant pled guilty to a statutorily defined sexually violent crime. His extended post-release supervision period imposed pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3717(d)(1)(D)(i) did not offend Apprendi.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the extended post-release supervision term and vacated as to the upward departure sentence for attempted rape and remanded for resentencing within the statutory range.

 

361 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


State v. Walker


No. 86,514


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


275 Kan. 46; 60 P.3d 937; 2003 Kan. LEXIS 3



January 10, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in an unpublished opinion filed May 24, 2002. Appeal from Sedgwick district court; WARREN M. WILBERT, judge.
State v. Walker, 47 P.3d 430, 2002 Kan. App. LEXIS 513 (Kan. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals vacating sentence and remanding for resentencing is reversed. Judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the Sedgwick District Court, Kansas, to aggravated indecent liberties with a child and received a presumptive prison term and an extended postrelease supervision term pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3717 (2001 Supp.). In an unpublished opinion the Court of Appeals, Kansas, vacated the postrelease term. The State petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aggravated indecent liberties with a child. In exchange for his guilty plea, the State agreed to recommend a presumptive prison sentence and not seek a departure. The trial court imposed a presumptive prison term of 61 months and a postrelease supervision term of 60 months based on the "nature of the offense." On appeal defendant argued that the district court based its postrelease departure on the fact that the crime was sexually motivated, a fact not admitted by defendant as part of his guilty plea. The State argued that defendant's extended postrelease period did not violate Apprendi and Gould. The appellate court held that a plea of guilty to a statutorily defined sexually violent crime provided the basis for an extended postrelease supervision period under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3717(d)(1)(D)(i) (2001 Supp.) without resort to court-made fact-findings, and thus that defendant's extended postrelease supervision period imposed under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3717(d)(1)(D)(i) did not offend Apprendi and Gould.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals vacating defendant's postrelease term and remanding for resentencing was reversed, and the judgment of the district court imposing an extended postrelease supervision term was affirmed.

Lacy v. Kan. Dental Bd.


No. 87,875


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 1031; 58 P.3d 668; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 780



December 6, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court; JAN W. LEUENBERGER, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Kansas Dental Board brought a disciplinary action against appellant dentist. The administrative law judge (ALJ) found that the dentist violated the law and suspended him from the practice of dentistry. The board affirmed the ALJ's ruling. The dentist appealed to the Shawnee District Court (Kansas), which affirmed the board's ruling. The dentist sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The dentist was found to have violated Kan. Stat. Ann. §§ 65-1435(c), 65-1436(a)(1), (13) based on false or misleading information placed on claim forms submitted to a dental insurer and the fact that the dentist conducted a dental office without being present for a majority of the hours that it was open. The Kansas Supreme Court found that: (1) each of the administrative law judge's (ALJ's) findings and conclusions were clearly supported by substantial competent evidence; (2) there was substantial competent evidence that that the dentist conducted a dental office in the name of the licensee when he was not personally present, which violated Kan. Stat. Ann. § 65-1435(c); (3) the ALJ, the board, and the district court were correct in their construction and application of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 65-1435(c); and (4) there was substantial competent evidence showing that the dentist violated Kan. Stat. Ann. § 65-1436(a)(1), (a)(13), and the subsequent imposition of the suspension was authorized by Kan. Stat. Ann. § 65-1436(b)(2).


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Krovvidi


No. 88,030


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 1059; 58 P.3d 687; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 783



December 6, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Johnson district court, JOHN ANDERSON III, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his sentence and conviction for vehicular homicide in the Johnson District Court, Kansas. The appeal was transferred pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 20-3018(c).


OVERVIEW: Following a bench trial, the district court found that defendant's running a red light caused an accident resulting in the death of the driver of another car. The district court concluded that the running of the red light, with no indication of other recklessness or impairment, satisfied the necessary element of a "material deviation" from the standard of care required for a conviction of vehicular homicide under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3405. Defendant argued on appeal that the mere violation of a traffic statute or ordinance through inattention, without additional aggravating factors, did not support a conviction of vehicular homicide. The appellate court found that the amount of deviation from the standard of care was not sufficient to support defendant's conviction for vehicular homicide where defendant had not been drinking and was not under the influence of any drug, none of his passengers warned him as he was about to enter the intersection or were concerned that his driving appeared reckless or that he was accelerating or speeding as he approached the intersection, and defendant, who was not speeding, proceeded through the intersection thinking his light was green.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded with instructions to vacate defendant's sentence.

 

365 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


State v. Armbrust


Nos. 88,264, 88,265, 88,266, 88,575


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 1089; 59 P.3d 1000; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 784



December 6, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court; MATTHEW J. DOWD, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted of crimes that required registration as a sex offender. The State charged each defendant with failing to comply with mandatory periodic address verification, the penalty for which had been changed from a misdemeanor to a felony since their convictions. The Shawnee District Court, Kansas, dismissed the complaints on the ground that the enhanced penalty was prohibited by the Ex Post Facto Clause. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: In a consolidated appeal, the State argued that the key date for purposes of an ex post facto analysis was not the date of conviction of the crime requiring registration, but rather the date when defendants were alleged to have violated the registration statute. The evidence showed that the actual crimes with which defendants were charged occurred after the effective date of the amendment of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-4903, which increased the penalty from a misdemeanor to a felony in 1999. Defendants were alleged to have failed to return address verification forms in June 2000 and thereafter. Thus, the supreme court determined that they could have conformed their conduct to the requirements of the amended registration statutes. The crime defendants were charged with was classed as a felony at the time each defendant allegedly committed it. Thus, the punishment had not been made more burdensome for defendants' violations of registration requirements after they failed to return the verification forms.


OUTCOME: The judgments were reversed and remanded with instructions to reinstate the charges against defendants.

 

366 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


State v. Long


No. 88,442


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 1095; 58 P.3d 706; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 785



December 6, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Ellsworth district court, BARRY A. BENNINGTON, judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Among several traffic citations, defendant was charged with having no liability insurance in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-3104 when he was driving a car he did not own. With the understanding that defendant was charged with a violation of subsection (d) of that statute, the Ellsworth District Court, Kansas, dismissed the charge. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the supreme court found that the questions reserved by the State assumed that defendant was charged under the provisions of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-3104(d). However, the arresting officer referred to the statute without citing the specific subsection; thus, the charging document was sufficient to charge defendant, who was not the owner of the vehicle, with a violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-3104(c). The supreme court found that the facts surrounding the issuance of the citation supported this conclusion as defendant handed the officer a document indicating that the insurance on the vehicle had expired three weeks before. Given the fact that the questions reserved by the State related to a charge not actually involved in this case, the supreme court concluded that the trial court's disposition under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-3104(d) did not amount to an adverse legal ruling on issues of statewide interest important to the correct and uniform administration of the state's criminal laws. Therefore, dismissal was proper. Further, the alternative ruling of the trial court on the constitutionality of § 40-3104(d) was not properly before the supreme court.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

In re City of Wichita


No. 85,953


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 915; 59 P.3d 336; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 787



December 6, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at In re City of Wichita, 2004 Kan. LEXIS 142 (Kan., Mar. 19, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in an unpublished opinion filed November 2, 2001. Appeal from the Board of Tax Appeals.
In re Appeal of City of Wichita, 35 P.3d 289, 2001 Kan. App. LEXIS 1053 (Kan. Ct. App., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals is affirmed in part and reversed in part. Judgment of the Board of Tax Appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a controversy between appellant city and appellee Kansas Department of Revenue involving a sales tax assessment for electricity consumed by the city in its delivery of water, the Kansas Court of Appeals reversed the Kansas Board of Tax Appeals' decision that additional retailers sales tax upon the electricity was due on the basis that to do otherwise denied the city equal protection under the United States Constitution. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: A water treatment plant owned by the city provided water for the dual purpose of fire protection and furnishing water to consumers. The department conducted an audit of the city's electricity purchases used to power the treatment plant for the period of June 1, 1992, through May 31, 1995. Although requested to do so, the department declined to segregate the electricity purchases according to the percentage of the water used for governmental purposes and the percentage of the water sold to consumers. The department concluded that a 2.5 percent rate of taxation applied and found that the city's purchases for the period of time in question did not qualify for partial exemption from the sales tax. The instant court concluded that the city's equal protection argument failed because the city did not demonstrate that the treatment it received under the state's tax laws was the result of intentional systematic unequal treatment. Because the city was in the business of furnishing water, any electricity purchases used for that purpose did not qualify for the sale tax exemption. The board was correct in not prorating the purchases and in refusing to waive interest on the assessed tax.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals' decision was affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the decision of the board was affirmed. The court of appeals' finding of a violation of equal protection was reversed, but its denial of attorney fees to the city was affirmed.

State v. Hurla


No. 87,852


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 725; 56 P.3d 252; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 684



October 25, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court, MATTHEW J. DOWD, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Shawnee District Court, Kansas, which dismissed a criminal complaint against defendant, who had been charged with burglary of a nondwelling, felony theft, and criminal damage to property. The case was transferred to the instant court on its own motion, pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 20-3018(c).


OVERVIEW: In September 1999, defendant was charged. In October 1999, defendant entered into a diversion agreement with the State. The agreement had a 24-month term. In August 2001, defendant filed a motion for early successful discharge from diversion. The State objected to the early termination. On appeal, the State argued that the district court lacked authority to dismiss the complaint. Defendant argued that the State's notice of appeal was fatally flawed as the State failed to specify what it was appealing. The instant court concluded that the State's notice of appeal was sufficient to invoke the jurisdiction of the court of appeals as a matter of right from the dismissal of the complaint. The matter was before the instant court on a valid transfer from the court of appeals. Defendant's challenge to the instant court's jurisdiction to hear the State's appeal was without merit. The district court had no jurisdiction to dismiss the complaint over the State's objection because the 24-month term of the diversion agreement had not been successfully completed. There was nothing in the diversion agreement authorizing a shortening of the term of the agreement except to go to trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded with directions to reinstate the diversion agreement and for a hearing to determine whether defendant had successfully completed the term of the diversion agreement.

State v. Beasley


No. 87,786


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 718; 56 P.3d 803; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 686



October 25, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Geary district court; STEVEN L. HORNBAKER, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Geary District Court (Kansas) which convicted him of aggravated assault by use of a hand gun and aggravated battery. The district court found that a firearm was used in the commission of the crimes and, under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4704a(h) (Supp. 2001), imposed two 12-month prison terms.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a group of men went to the victim's home. Defendant and one other man hit, kicked, and threatened the victim with a gun, while the other men took the victim's television, VCR, and microwave. The prosecutor referred to defendant's role in robbing the victim in cross-examination of witness's and in closing argument. The jury found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant used a firearm to commit the aggravated assault. The Kansas Supreme Court found that: (1) the prosecutor's questioning of witnesses was not improper and it did not amount to misconduct, (2) the prosecutor's closing argument was fair comment on the evidence produced at trial, and (3) Apprendi did not apply to the mandatory imposition of a prison term under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4704a(h) (Supp. 2001) because the prison term did not exceed the statutory maximum punishment for defendant's crime.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was affirmed.

Lower v. Bd. of Dirs.


No. 87,863


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 735; 56 P.3d 235; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 687



October 25, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Haskell district court; KIM R. SCHROEDER, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cemetery lot owners challenged a decision of the Haskell District Court (Kansas), which granted appellee county cemetery district board of directors summary judgment, issued a permanent injunction against the owners, and ordered the owners to remove a monument they erected. The matter came before the court pursuant to a transfer.


OVERVIEW: The owners purchased a cemetery lot to erect a monument memorializing unborn babies as a class. The owners did not plan to bury anyone in the lot. The board requested that the monument be removed. The owners then brought the action, but the trial court found in favor of the board. The court affirmed on appeal. The trial court did not err in determining that, in light of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 17-1302, the monument violated statutory authority because it was used for a purpose other than sepulture. The trial court did not err in granting summary judgment against the owners on their claim that the board violated Kan. Const. Bill Rights § 7 because the record did not show that the owners were coerced into acting in a manner contrary to their beliefs as a result of the board's actions. The court held that neither state laws nor the board's actions regarding the removal of the monument constituted a taking of the owners' property interest in the lot in violation of due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision in favor of the board.

State v. Moore


No. 86,630


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 639; 55 P.3d 903; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 695



October 25, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Geary district court, LARRY E. BENGTSON, judge.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's convictions affirmed; sentences vacated; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Geary District Court, Kansas, convicted defendant of one count of aggravated indecent liberties with a child, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3504(a)(3)(A), and one count of kidnapping, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3420(b). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the district court erred in its response to a question submitted by the jury. The appellate court found that aggravated indecent liberties, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3504(a)(3)(A), required a touching. The videotaping of a child did not constitute a touching. The jury's question was covered by the court's instruction. The prosecutor sought to show that defendant's version of events was not feasible based on the victim's testimony at trial. Under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-455, defendant's prior convictions were relevant as the two present crimes at issue were similar to his previous convictions. The alleged conduct squarely contradicted the issues of identity, motive, preparation, and plan and placed them in issue. The evidence supporting the conviction was sufficient to convict defendant. The district court erred in failing to remove from defendant's criminal history the sexually violent crime it used to qualify him as a persistent sex offender under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4704(j) (Supp. 1997). The district court was not required to make factual findings beyond the existence of the convictions because all the crimes were defined as sexually violent crimes.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the convictions and reversed and remanded as to sentencing.

State v. Garcia


No. 87,691


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 708; 56 P.3d 797; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 698



October 25, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Ford district court, DANIEL L. LOVE, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Ford District Court, Kansas, convicted defendant of aggravated robbery, a security level 7 felony, and one count of incitement to riot, a severity level 8 felony, in exchange for the dismissal of the remaining charges. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the fact the crimes were gang related, Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4704a(k) (Supp. 2001), had to be proven to a jury beyond a reasonable doubt before that fact could be used to impose a prison term rather than probation. The appellate court found that the district court's conclusion that defendant's crimes were gang related, triggering a presumptive prison sentence, did not increase the penalty for his crimes beyond the statutory maximum. Upon finding that the crimes were gang related, the district court imposed a presumptive prison term. The district court failed to make adequate findings on the record to support imposition of a prison term based on the fact that the crimes were gang related. The language of § 21-4704a(k) contained an explicit statement of the showing required to trigger the presumptive prison sentence, including the defendant's specific intent to promote or assist certain conduct by gang members. The district court at the second sentencing hearing did not mention the statute. The district court did not find that defendant's crimes were committed for the benefit of, at the direction of, or in association with any criminal street gang.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the convictions and vacated as to defendant's sentences and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Carr


No. 85,238


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 442; 53 P.3d 843; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 547



September 13, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 29 Kan. App. 2d 501, 28 P.3d 436 (2001). Appeal from Sedgwick district court; DAVID W. KENNEDY and GREGORY L. WALLER, judges.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals affirmed. Judgment of the district court reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with criminal possession of a firearm. Defendant entered into a plea agreement with the State, where the State would recommend a mid-range sentence, no fine and probation. The trial court, based on defendant's criminal history, sentenced him to 15 months and refused to grant probation. The Kansas Court of Appeals held there were substantial and compelling reasons for the upward dispositional departure. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested 26 days after his release from a youth facility where he served a sentence arising from an adjudication on drug charges. Defendant was pulled over because he was driving without a vehicle license tag. When defendant admitted to driving on a suspended license, he was placed in custody, and the car was searched. A stolen gun was found in the passenger compartment. The trial court noted that defendant's criminal history and the severity score of the charged crime and, without notice, sentenced defendant to 15 months and refused to grant parole. The state supreme court affirmed the court of appeals and held that that United States Supreme Court decision in Apprendi did not apply to upward dispositional departures, as it would require a jury to make a finding beyond a reasonable doubt before any defendant falling within a presumptive probation gridbox could be denied probation. The court also held that while the trial court had substantial and compelling reasons for the upward dispositional departure based on the short time between defendant's release and his arrest, the case had to be remanded as the trial court did not give notice of its intention to depart.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Court of Appeals vacating defendant's sentence and remanding for resentencing was affirmed because the district court failed to give adequate notice of its intent to depart. The judgment of the district court was reversed.

Winston v. State Dep't of Soc. & Rehab. Servs.


No. 87,820


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 396; 49 P.3d 1274; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 482



July 19, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Winston v. Kan. Dep't of Soc. & Rehab., 2002 U.S. LEXIS 9275 (U.S. Dec. 16, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Johnson district court; JOHN P. BENNETT, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a decision of the Johnson District Court (Kansas), which affirmed a state appeals committee's decision that affirmed the ruling of appellee Kansas Department of Social and Rehabilitation Services (SRS), which found that the father physically abused his son and emotionally abused his son and daughter.


OVERVIEW: The SRS conducted an investigation of allegations that the father was abusing his son. The father was also investigated for abusing his daughter. During the course of the proceedings, he was interviewed by law enforcement officials. The SRS's substantiation and validation of the father regarding the physical abuse of his son and the emotional abuse of his son and his daughter were affirmed. The district court affirmed the decision. The supreme court held that the SRS did not fail to follow prescribed procedures, nor were its procedures in violation of Kansas law. There was no error in the procedure that allowed law enforcement to interview the father as an alleged perpetrator. This procedure was supported by Kan. Admin. Regs. § 30-46-13(a) and Kan. Stat. Ann. § 38-1523(b). The father's due process rights were not violated. While a protected liberty interest was involved, because that interest was not to be abridged until after the father exhausted his appeals, in that his name was not to be placed on a child abuse registry until that time, there was no constitutional violation. There was substantial evidence to support the abuse allegations.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the decision that the father abused his son and daughter.

Plains Petroleum Co. v. First Nat'l Bank of Lamar


No. 86,614


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 74; 49 P.3d 432; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 427; 158 Oil & Gas Rep. 289



July 12, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Stevens district court; TOM R. SMITH, judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeals dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff oil producers were directed to pay ad valorem taxes plus interest from 1983 to 1988. The producers sued defendant royalty owners for reimbursement of the taxes. The royalty owners claimed that the producers' claim was time barred by Kan. Stat. Ann. § 55-1624 (2001 Supp.). The Stevens District Court (Kansas) denied the producers' motion for summary judgment and they appealed.


OVERVIEW: Each of the producers in its docketing statement answered affirmatively the question whether the order appealed from was a final order. Each indicated that invocation of the provisions of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-254(b) (2001 Supp.) was "not applicable." Finally, in response to the question relating to statutory authority for appeal, each producer responded that the specific authority for its direct appeal was Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-2101(b). The trial court then appeared to acknowledge that there was at least one additional legal issue which remained to be resolved in the case at bar. The Supreme Court of Kansas's concern that the decision in the case at bar was not one which finally resolved all of the issues was strengthened when at oral argument counsel for the royalty owners admitted the recoupment and right to setoff issues remained and even if the statute of limitations had run the right of the producers to recover was still in issue. The trial court's decision and journal entry that its order was final and appealable was legally incorrect. It was not a final order. The supreme court did not have jurisdiction over the appeals or the cross-appeals.


OUTCOME: The appeals were dismissed.

State v. Papen


No. 87,000


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 149; 50 P.3d 37; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 450



July 12, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Papen v. Kansas, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 8881 (U.S. Dec. 2, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Sedgwick district court; DAVID W. KENNEDY, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas) of premeditated first-degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in responding to the jury's request regarding the read back of the testimony of a witness who testified regarding the timing of events, because the jury's request was not satisfied, as the read back did not inform them that the testimony was only an approximation of the time. The supreme court disagreed. Contrary to defendant's position, the read-back testimony clearly and repeatedly stated that the times were approximations. The witness was asked approximately when he went on the first errand, and he responded that he left about 2 and returned at approximately 3 or 3:30. Regarding the second errand, the witness said that he left at approximately 4 and that he was not gone more than an hour, if that long. Defendant's admission on cross-examination that he was "guesstimating" was nothing more than a slight variation on the testimony that was read back to the jury. The read-back provided by the trial court satisfied the jury request insofar as it involved the times of the witness's errands. Therefore, the trial court did not err.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

377 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


State v. Beard


No. 87,205


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 181; 49 P.3d 492; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 451



July 12, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sumner district court; THOMAS H. GRABER, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a ruling of the Sumner District Court, Kansas, which vacated defendant's sentence and held that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4603d(e) (Supp. 1999), a sentencing statute providing for placement by intervenor, the Kansas Department of Corrections, in a correctional conservation camp, was unconstitutional as a violation of separation of powers.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty two counts of sale of methamphetamine, pursuant to a plea agreement. The State and defendant agreed to recommend that the maximum sentence on each count was 23 months in prison and that the sentences were to run consecutively. The sentencing judge failed to comply with a statutory mandate to state on the record why defendant should not be placed in a correctional conservation camp or community intermediate sanction center. Subsequently, the department placed defendant placed in a correctional conservation camp. The sentencing judge concluded that defendant should not have been placed in the conservation camp. Both defendant and the department asserted that § 21-4603d(e) did not violate the doctrine of separation of powers and that the district court erred in finding the statute unconstitutional. The State, however, contended that the district court did not err in finding the statute unconstitutional. The instant court held that there was no violation of separation of powers that rendered § 21-4603d(e) constitutional. Although there was some blending of powers, the executive branch was not usurping the powers of the judicial branch.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded with instructions that defendant be placed in community corrections.

 

378 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


State v. Douglas


No. 86,740


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


274 Kan. 96; 49 P.3d 446; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 454



July 12, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied: Douglas v. Kansas, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 1262 (U.S. Feb. 24, 2003).
Writ of certiorari denied Douglas v. Kansas, 537 U.S. 1198, 123 S. Ct. 1268, 154 L. Ed. 2d 1037, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 1262 (2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Douglas v. State, 2006 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 632 (Kan. Ct. App., Mar. 31, 2006)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Douglas v. McKune, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 39508 (D. Kan., June 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court; TOM MALONE, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas) of two counts of premeditated first-degree murder and two counts of aggravated robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the prosecutor committed misconduct during closing arguments, which warranted reversal. The supreme court disagreed. It appeared that the prosecutor was attempting to show that defendant's version of the events was not practicable under the evidence presented at trial. The prosecutor's characterization of defendant's version of the facts as "unbelievable" did not rise to the level of the conduct in cited caselaw. When the prosecutor said defendant's story was "ridiculous, absurd, and ludicrous," the trial court instructed the jury to disregard the statement. While such a comment appeared improper, it did not deprive defendant of a fair trial. Near the end of closing arguments the prosecutor said, "in fact the detective can lie to a suspect, and it is perfectly acceptable, the detective could lie to all of us in an interview, but he did not about blood found on defendant's personal items." In context, it appeared the prosecutor was focusing on the importance of the blood evidence. Therefore, the prosecutor's comments were not misconduct, and they did not warrant reversal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

379 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


In re Gates


No. 87,713


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


273 Kan. 1025; 46 P.3d 1206; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 329



June 7, 2002 , Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Shawnee district court; TERRY L. BULLOCK, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant appealed a judgment of the Shawnee District Court, Kansas, which affirmed appellee Kansas Real Estate Commission's denial of a real estate license as a salesperson. The Kansas Court of Appeals transferred the case to the instant court.


OVERVIEW: The applicant, who pled guilty in March 1996 to a drug felony in federal court argued that the commission's decision denying his application was not supported by substantial evidence; was contrary to undisputed evidence; and was unreasonable, arbitrary, or capricious. The applicant's earlier license had expired in June 1997. The commission denied the application based on the seriousness of the applicant's misconduct and his subsequent conduct. The instant court observed that there were no facts in the record that supported the commission's finding that the applicant was not rehabilitated. In fact, the evidence relevant to rehabilitation tended to show that the applicant was a useful and law-abiding member of society. The fact that the applicant was on supervised release was not, in and of itself, subsequent conduct of the applicant. Kan. Stat. Ann. § 58-3043(a) required the commission to balance the applicant's conviction with other factors. However, it did not appear that the commission did so. The determination regarding the applicant's subsequent conduct was not substantially supported by evidence in the record. Thus, the commission's decision was arbitrary and unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the case was remanded to the commission with directions to make findings of fact based on substantial competent evidence consistent with the instant court's opinion.

 

380 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


State v. Albright


No. 85,599


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


273 Kan. 811; 46 P.3d 1167; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 307



May 31, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Albright v. Kansas, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 7495 (U.S. Oct. 15, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Sedgwick district court; WARREN M. WILBERT, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas) of first-degree premeditated murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by allowing his expert witness to testify regarding defendant's prior conduct. The supreme court disagreed. Before reaching his conclusions, the expert reviewed defendant's previous hospitalization information, military records, some psychiatric records, family history, police reports, witness statements, and police reports from past incidents. Regarding defendant's mental condition at the time of the victim's murder, the expert testified that defendant was psychotic, delusional, and suffering from paranoid schizophrenia. The State, on cross-examination, inquired about the information the expert had reviewed. The evidence was admitted to show errors in the expert's understanding of events upon which he based his opinion and to show the facts upon which he based his conclusions. The prosecutor was allowed to test the reasonableness of the expert's opinion during a proper cross-examination. Once the issue was raised on direct examination, the door was open, and cross-examination was not restricted to the identical details developed on direct examination or the specific facts testified to in direct examination.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Lietz Constr. Co.


No. 86,987


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


273 Kan. 890; 47 P.3d 1275; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 310



May 31, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Board of Tax Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county imposed an ad valorem property tax on equipment owned by appellee company. The Board of Tax Appeals (BOTA) (Kansas) granted the company's request for a tax exemption. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company owned bulldozers, dirt scrapers, a road grader, an excavator, and the trailers for which it sought a tax exemption from ad valorem property tax. The company was a soil conservation contractor and provided evidence that the equipment was used to do work for farmers and ranchers as well as any other dirt work. BOTA held that the equipment was actually and regularly used as farm equipment and was exempted from tax under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 79-201j(a). The appellate court affirmed the finding of BOTA that the company's equipment constituted farming equipment as soil conservation measures were generally understood to be an integral part of current farming practices. The court also held that § 79-201j was not unconstitutionally vague as the definition of "farm equipment" that included property that was actually and regularly used in any farming or ranching operation including the performing of farm or ranch work for hire was sufficient.


OUTCOME: The decision of BOTA was affirmed.

In re Marriage of Rayman


No. 88,051


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


273 Kan. 996; 47 P.3d 413; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 312



May 31, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wyandotte district court; DANIEL DUNCAN, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wyandotte District Court, Kansas, ordered continued residential custody of the parties' children in appellee husband. Appellant wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The wife argued the trial court misapplied Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-1610(a)(2) (2001 Supp.) and the parental preference doctrine, and abused its discretion in failing to find a material change of circumstances occurred and the best interest of the children would be served by changing residential custody to her during the husband's one-year Korean military tour of duty. The appellate court found that the argument in the wife's brief of an unconstitutional application of the statute was not made to the trial court, and thus was not properly before the appellate court for review. The issues before the trial court did involve the application of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-1610(a)(2) (2001 Supp.). The residential custody was continued in the father, although he enjoyed the assistance of his present wife in caring for the children, the residential custody was and remained with the father. The temporary transfer of a parent with residential custody did not automatically trigger a custody change. There was substantial and competent evidence to support the trial court's findings and rulings.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Anthony


No. 86,674


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


273 Kan. 726; 45 P.3d 852; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 194



May 7, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wyandotte district court; THOMAS L. BOEDING, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; sentence vacated, and case remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Wyandotte District Court (Kansas), convicting him of aggravated indecent liberties with a child and sentencing him to 92 months' incarceration, to be followed by a period of postrelease supervision of 60 months.


OVERVIEW: The period of supervision was extended from 36 to 60 months based on the district court judge's post-conviction findings. Defendant argued the extended period of postrelease supervision constituted an unconstitutional upward durational departure. Defendant argued the district court imposed an upward durational departure sentence by subjecting him to the extended postrelease supervision period. The statutory maximum penalty for defendant's crime included a 36-month postrelease period. The supreme court ruled the district court's extension of defendant's postrelease period from 36 to 60 months increased the penalty for his crime beyond the statutory maximum. However, the conviction of aggravated indecent liberties constituted a substantial and compelling reason to impose the postrelease supervision departure and was an acceptable departure. Furthermore, the district court must rely on sentencing guidelines in effect on the date of the offense and erred when it looked to the presumptive range on the date of sentencing.


OUTCOME: The period of postrelease supervision was affirmed, the underlying sentence of imprisonment was vacated, and the case was remanded for resentencing.

State v. Cope


No. 84,221


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


273 Kan. 642; 44 P.3d 1224; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 165



April 26, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in 29 Kan. App. 2d. ___, 29 P.3d 974 (2001). Appeal from Johnson district court, DAVID L. KENNEDY, assigned judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals reversing the district court is reversed. Judgment of the district court is affirmed. The case is remanded to the Court of Appeals for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kansas Court of Appeals reversed the trial court's conviction of defendant of making a criminal threat, pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3419(a)(1). The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant. The appellate court found that the determination of whether the statements were made in reckless disregard of the risk of causing an evacuation of the courthouse was the primary issue for the jury to decide. Regardless of whether the threat was real or even capable of being carried out, it was the reaction desired by the communicator, or the communicator's reckless disregard of the possibility of creating that reaction which constituted the offense. Defendant told the witness that he was ready to assault the courthouse, and came across as an angry, desperate man on the edge of losing all control. There was nothing in the circumstances or actual statements made other than defendant's testimony at trial that supported his contention that the whole thing was a joke on his part. Defendant had elaborated his plan to the witness, and the fact that subsequent investigations revealed no evidence of defendant's capability to carry out his threats was not a factor in determining whether or not the threat was made in reckless disregard of the risk.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Am. Trust Adm'Rs v. Sebelius


No. 86,801


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


273 Kan. 694; 44 P.3d 1253; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 168



April 26, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Johnson district court, JOHN P. BENNETT, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: With its first suit resolved, appellant insurer continued its second suit for approval of its policy. Appellee commissioner entered a final order against the insurer. The insurer appealed, and the Johnson County District Court, Kansas, rejected all of the insurer's arguments, except the collateral estoppel argument. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insurer sought to gain the insurance commissioner's approval of its stop-loss insurance policy. The commissioner refused to approve the policy. The insurer alleged on appeal that: (1) the commissioner did not have jurisdiction to regulate stop-loss policies; (2) the commissioner's regulation failed to comply with the Kansas statutory rules governing regulatory procedure; (3) the regulation was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power; and (4) federal law preempted the commissioner's regulation of the policy. The commissioner alleged that the insurer was collaterally estopped from asserting the preemption issue. The supreme court held: (1) the commissioner had statutory authority under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 40-2201(b) to require minimum attachment points for stop-loss insurance policies; (2) the commissioner's attempt to regulate stop-loss policies was void for failure to comply with Kan. Stat. Ann. § 77-415 et seq.; (3) the insurer's unconstitutional delegation of power claim was not preserved for appeal; and (4) since the commissioner's bulletin had no force, there was no regulation to be preempted by federal law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded as to the commissioner's use of a general bulletin instead of a statutory rule or regulation.

 

386 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


State v. Watson


No. 86,622


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


273 Kan. 426; 44 P.3d 357; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 142



April 19, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Pratt district court; ROBERT J. SCHMISSEUR, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pratt District Court, Kansas, convicted defendant of attempting to smuggle contraband into the county jail. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-3826 (2001 Supp.). She conceded that the statute was constitutional as applied, but contended that it was facially unconstitutional. A criminal statute was unconstitutionally vague and indefinite unless its language conveyed a sufficiently definite warning of the conduct proscribed when measured by common understanding and practice. The appellate court found that a statute was not necessarily vague or overbroad simply because the legislature delegated the authority to determine what items constituted contraband to an agent or an agency. Procedural safeguards had to be in place in order to ensure that the statute was implemented in a constitutional manner. Due process required nondeceptive notice such that every person was able to know with certainty when he or she was committing a crime. The statute was not constitutionally inadequate on its face. The statute did not unlawfully delegate legislative authority in violation of the separation of powers doctrine, as a similar federal statute, 18 U.S.C.S. § 1791 had withstood various constitutional challenges based upon the separation of powers doctrine.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Easterwood v. State


No. 86,325


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


273 Kan. 361; 44 P.3d 1209; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 143



April 19, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Easterwood v. Kansas, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 7649 (U.S. Oct. 15, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wyandotte district court; JOHN J. BUKATY, JR., judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant pleaded guilty in the Wyandotte District Court (Kansas) to, inter alia, felony murder. He filed a motion for postconviction relief, which was denied. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion for postconviction relief, because under the Kansas Supreme Court's interpretation of felony murder, the defendant did not commit felony murder. The defendant argued that an opinion interpreting felony murder that was issued while the appeal was pending should have been retroactively applied to the defendant's postconviction motion. The supreme court disagreed. The decision should not have been retroactively applied as a matter of public policy under all the facts of the case. There clearly was a factual basis for the trial court to accept the defendant's plea. The trial court heard sufficient evidence from counsel's testimony to uphold the trial court's findings that the defendant was sufficiently advised of the potential penalties that he faced at the time of his plea. The defendant knowingly decided to take advantage of the favorable plea agreement. He was not coerced or pushed into doing so. He made the best of what was not a good situation that had every possibility of becoming much worse. Therefore, the trial court did not err by denying the motion for postconviction relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Hudson v. State


No. 86,437


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


273 Kan. 251; 42 P.3d 150; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 116



March 15, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Hudson v. Koener, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 14659 (D. Kan., June 25, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court; PAUL W. CLARK, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4608(f)(5), a prisoner received no credit for time spent on parole on the aggregate sentence imposed when she committed a new offense while on parole. The Sedgwick District Court (Kansas) granted relief under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 60-1507, finding that the denial of credit was a violation of the Constitution's prohibition against double jeopardy and its requirement of due process.


OVERVIEW: The question on appeal was whether Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4608(f)(5) was unconstitutional as a violation of the Fifth Amendment guarantee against double jeopardy and guarantee of due process and whether it conflicted with Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3722. The State contended that the prisoner was not being punished twice for the same offense but was serving an enhanced sentence for the new crime. The appellate court held that the forfeiture of credit for time served on parole under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4608(f)(5) did not violate the prisoner's procedural due process rights. The consequences of § 21-4608(f)(5) did not affect her until consecutive sentences were imposed for committing a new offense while on parole. The prisoner had fair notice. The amendment was effective for nearly eight years before she committed the act which triggered its application. No additional punishment was inflicted upon the prisoner by virtue of § 21-4608(f)(5). The prisoner was returned to prison to complete her original sentence and her new sentence. There was no double jeopardy or due process issue. Section 21-4608(f)(5) was not unconstitutional nor did it conflict with Kan. Stat. Ann. § 22-3722.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

 

389 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hitt


No. 85,553


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


273 Kan. 224; 42 P.3d 732; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 121



March 15, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Hitt v. Kansas, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 582 (U.S. Jan. 13, 2003).


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in an unpublished decision filed August 24, 2001. Appeal from Lyon district court; MERLIN G. WHEELER, judge.

 State v. Hitt, 30 P.3d 1058, 2001 Kan. App. LEXIS 820 (Kan. Ct. App. 2001) 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals affirming the district court is affirmed. Judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant argued that the trial court should not have included his juvenile adjudications in his criminal history because they were the result of proceedings in which he did not have the right to a jury trial. The Court of Appeals decided that defendant's juvenile adjudications were correctly included in his Kansas Sentencing Guidelines Act (KSGA), specifically Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4704 (2001 Supp.), criminal history score. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that juvenile adjudications included in a criminal history score increased the penalty for a crime beyond the prescribed statutory maximum. He reasoned that under Apprendi, juvenile adjudications had to be charged in the indictment and proven to a jury beyond a reasonable doubt. Because the KSGA provided that juvenile adjudications could be included in the criminal history score absent those requirements, he contended the KSGA was unconstitutional on its face and as applied to his sentence. The supreme court held that Apprendi created an exception allowing the use of a prior conviction to increase a defendant's sentence based on the historical role of recidivism in the sentencing decision and on the procedural safeguards attached to prior convictions. Juvenile adjudications were included within the historical cloak of recidivism and enjoyed ample procedural safeguards; the Apprendi exception for prior convictions encompassed juvenile adjudications. Juvenile adjudications did not have to be charged in an indictment or proven to a jury beyond a reasonable doubt before they could be used in calculating a defendant's criminal history score under the KSGA.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court and the judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed.

State v. Boorigie


No. 85,604


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


273 Kan. 18; 41 P.3d 764; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 80

Post-conviction relief denied at Boorigie v. State, 2010 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 498 (Kan. Ct. App., July 9, 2010)

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, arson, impairing a security interest, and six counts of criminal solicitation, and he was sentenced to life. The Montgomery District Court (Kansas) also ordered an upward durational departure on the arson charge. The sentences were ordered to run consecutively. OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering his wife and then setting fire to her house. The autopsy showed that she died of manual strangulation prior to the fire. There was also evidence that his wife was lifted up by her neck. The supreme court held that venue in Montgomery County was proper, because it was the county where the defendant faced the original charges and it was the place where crimes were committed for which defendant solicited false testimony. OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed, the sentences were vacated in part, and case was remanded with directions.

State v. Bramlett


No. 86,138


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


273 Kan. 67; 41 P.3d 796; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 122



March 8, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in an unpublished decision filed Appeal from Wyandotte district court; JOHN J. MCNALLY, judge.

 State v. Bramlett, 28 P.3d 1066, 2001 Kan. App. LEXIS 765 (Kan. Ct. App. 2001) 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant pled guilty to seven sex crimes. The Wyandotte Count District Court (Kansas) ordered four of the seven sentences to run consecutively. The defendant appealed the sentences. The Kansas Court of Appeals dismissed the case on the basis that it had no jurisdiction to review a presumptive sentence and rejected the argument that the sentence was unconstitutional under Apprendi v. New Jersey. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the defendant raised the sole question of whether, under Apprendi, his constitutional rights were violated when the district court imposed consecutive sentences. The defendant asserted that the grounds on which the district court relied for imposing consecutive sentences, failure to fully accept his responsibility, were the same factual grounds the court rejected in denying the upward departure. The supreme court found no Apprendi violation and affirmed the court of appeals. In Apprendi, the United States Supreme Court held that, other than the fact of a prior conviction, any fact that increased the penalty for a crime beyond the prescribed statutory maximum must be submitted to a jury and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. The supreme court found that the presumptive sentence imposed for each count was within the applicable sentencing guideline. The district court did not exceed the maximum sentence for any individual count. Therefore, it could not be said that, as to any individual count, the district court's findings resulted in the imposition of a greater punishment than was authorized by the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed.

SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed tax protests involving eight tracts of pastureland situated in one county. State v. Roberson


No. 84,640


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


272 Kan. 1143; 38 P.3d 715; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 3

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wyandotte district court; CORDELL D. MEEKS, JR., judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree premeditated murder in the Wyandotte District Court (Kansas) and was sentenced to a hard 40 with 141 additional months to run consecutively. Defendant appealed, alleging the trial court erred in failing to provide the jury with a verdict form that allowed the jury to find defendant not guilty of premeditated first-degree murder due to mental disease or defect. Defendant alleged numerous other errors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for the murder of his girlfriend. Ann. § 21-4635(a) or notice of the aggravating factors on which it would rely, because evidence presented by the State at trial was known to defendant and was admissible for hard 40 sentencing purposes. Finally, the supreme court held portions of defendant's diary regarding his volatile relationship with the victim was admissible to show motive and intent.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Nat'l Compressed Steel Corp. v. Unified Gov't of Wyandotte County/Kansas City


No. 86,401


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


272 Kan. 1239; 38 P.3d 723; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 11



January 25, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wyandotte district court; PHILIP L. SIEVE, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company sought to enjoin the appellee county from undertaking an environmental examination of the company's property in conjunction with a pending eminent domain action initiated to acquire real property owned by the company. The Wyandotte District Court denied the company's petition for a permanent injunction. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county moved for an order to allow entry upon the company's land to perform environmental testing. The district court order allowed the county to enter the company's property to perform the environmental testing without requiring an easement or paying the company for the use of its land. The company argued that the statutory authority that allowed the county to enter its property and conduct tests in an eminent domain proceeding did not include the right to perform extensive environmental testing. The company argued also that it was inappropriate to have the same judge sit for both the condemnation proceeding and the injunction petition. The state supreme court held it did not create a conflict to allow a judge to sit in both proceedings and review his own orders. The court found the company met the elements to obtain an injunction, as the testing and its results could cause the company to suffer irreparable harm that would affect the ongoing nature of its business. As the county proposed the testing not to correct an environmental problem, but to determine the economic viability of the land, no statutory authority existed to allow the subsurface testing to occur.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of the company's petition for injunction was reversed.

 

396 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


In re Appeal of Panhandle E. Pipe Line Co.


No. 86,277


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


272 Kan. 1211; 39 P.3d 21; 2002 Kan. LEXIS 8



January 25, 2002, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Board of Tax Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees parent company and subsidiary company (companies) sought to file a combined tax return and obtain a refund for prior years. The appellant department of revenue (department) denied their request. The Board of Tax Appeals' (Kansas) issued a final order finding that respondents were a unitary business and could file a combined return. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The companies requested permission to amend corporate tax returns and to file a combined report as a unitary business. The department determined that the parent company could not establish its right to file a combined return, as it did not own more than 50 percent of the subsidiary company. The companies appealed the department's decision. The Board of Tax Appeals (BOTA) found that the operations of the two companies were functionally integrated and centrally managed by the parent company. The subsidiary company's operations were intertwined with the parent company to meet its necessary specifications for pipeline operations. The parent company also was the subsidiary company's sole source of legal, tax planning, preparation services, and helped with its employee stock plan. The department asserted its decision was entitled to judicial deference by BOTA. The appellate court held that BOTA properly applied a de novo standard of review to the department's decision. As Kansas did not apply a bright line test for a unitary business, and the two companies shared such an interdependent relationship so as to form one integral business, BOTA's determination was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The order of the Board of Tax Appeals was affirmed.

 

397 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kleypas


No. 80,920


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


272 Kan. 894; 40 P.3d 139; 2001 Kan. LEXIS 953



December 28, 2001, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 8, 2002. Second Correction March 21, 2002. Writ of certiorari denied: Kleypas v. Kansas, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6187 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002).
Writ of certiorari denied Kleypas v. Kansas, 537 U.S. 834, 123 S. Ct. 144, 154 L. Ed. 2d 53, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6187 (2002)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by State v. Kleypas, 282 Kan. 560, 147 P.3d 1058, 2006 Kan. LEXIS 716 (2006)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by State v. Kleypas, 2016 Kan. LEXIS 475 (Kan., Oct. 21, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Crawford district court, DONALD R. NOLAND, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, attempted rape, and burglary and sentenced to death. The Crawford District Court (Kansas) denied the defendant's motion for new trial and motion to recall the jurors. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant killed the victim after breaking into her home and trying to rape her. One of the aggravating factors that the jury considered was that the defendant killed the victim because she was able to identify him. The defendant raised 43 issues on appeal. The appellate court held that no errors were committed by the trial court with respect to the admission of the confession, the specificity of the search warrant, the determination of competency, the selection of jurors, the jury instructions, juror misconduct, or alleged prosecutorial misconduct, thus a new trial was not warranted. The appellate court held that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4624(e) was unconstitutional as applied; in that it required the jury to issue a death sentence, if they found that aggravating and mitigating factors were in equipoise. As such, the death sentence was vacated. The court also held that the verdict form also warranted vacating the death sentence, as the verdict form erroneously informed the jury that it had to unanimously agree that a sentence other than death should be imposed. The prosecutor's misconduct during closing arguments and sentencing did not constitute reversible error.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed. The death sentence was vacated, and the matter was remanded for a sentencing hearing consistent with the opinion.

 

398 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown


No. 86,130


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


272 Kan. 843; 35 P.3d 910; 2001 Kan. LEXIS 949



December 14, 2001, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Sedgwick district court, JOSEPH BRIBIESCA, judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction in the Sedgwick District Court (Kansas) on stipulated facts of one count of payment for adoption, in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 59-2121(a), and one count of prohibited offers and placement of children for adoption, in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 59-2123.


OVERVIEW: The stipulated facts were that defendant offered money and a new car to a former employee for the former employee's newborn child. The supreme court found it was clear that it was the legislative intent that all fees, expenses, or other consideration received not meeting one of the six exceptions provided for under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 59-2121(a) would be "clearly excessive" and a violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 59-2121(c), where the excessive fees or expenses were received or accepted knowingly or intentionally. The fact that defendant had not yet received the money she bargained for in brokering the child when law enforcement officials stepped in did not change the nature of the transaction. Defendant brokered a deal for the sale of the child in a three-way transaction. Defendant requested a fee for her services in putting the deal together. Buyers, seller, and broker accepted the terms thereof, and the child was transferred under the agreed-upon terms. Consequently, defendant's conduct constituted knowingly and intentionally receiving or accepting clearly excessive fees or expenses in violation of Kan. Stat. Ann. § 59-2121(a), as set forth in Kan. Stat. Ann. § 59-2121(c).


OUTCOME: The supreme court held the stipulated facts supported defendant's conviction.

 

399 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


State v. Flournoy


No. 84,042


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


272 Kan. 784; 36 P.3d 273; 2001 Kan. LEXIS 947



December 14, 2001, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Flournoy, 2003 Kan. Unpub. LEXIS 54 (Kan., Dec. 12, 2003)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Flournoy v. State, 2006 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1091 (Kan. Ct. App., Oct. 20, 2006)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Flournoy v. State, 2016 Kan. App. Unpub. LEXIS 795 (Kan. Ct. App., Sept. 30, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wyandotte district court; JOHN J. BUKATY, JR., judge.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed, sentence vacated, and case remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions entered in the Wyandotte District Court (Kansas) for first-degree premeditated murder of his grandmother and battery of his girlfriend. The district court imposed a hard 40 sentence under Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4636(c),(f), finding that the murder was a crime committed for the purpose of receiving money or other thing of monetary value and was committed in an especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel manner.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered his grandmother with five gunshots. On appeal, the first issue was whether there was sufficient evidence of aggravating circumstances for the imposition of the hard 40 sentence. The supreme court found that there was sufficient evidence to show that the murder was committed for the purpose of receiving money or any other thing for monetary value, an aggravating circumstance. However, the supreme court noted that shooting deaths were generally not considered committed in an especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel manner. The supreme court concluded that unlike the victims in other shooting death cases where a hard 40 sentence was imposed, the victim in the instant case was not chased down, nor forced to lie on the floor awaiting death. The shooting took place within 1 minute. Therefore, the evidence did not support a finding that the murder was committed in an especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel manner. Finally, the appellate court rejected defendant's claims that the district court erred in determining defendant's girlfriend, an eyewitness, was unavailable and allowed her preliminary hearing transcript to be used as evidence at trial.


OUTCOME: Defendant's hard 40 sentence was vacated, and the matter was remanded to the district court for reweighing of the one remaining aggravating circumstance and the mitigating circumstance of no significant history of prior criminal activity.

 

400 of 1638 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cody


Nos. 83,126, 83,686


SUPREME COURT OF KANSAS


272 Kan. 564; 35 P.3d 800; 2001 Kan. LEXIS 925



December 7, 2001, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals in State v. Cody, 27 Kan. App. 2d 1037, 10 P.3d 789, 2000 Kan. App. LEXIS 998 (2000). Appeal from Sedgwick district court; DAVID W. DEWEY, judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant pled guilty to drug possession charges, and was sentenced to 64 months, which was double the presumptive sentence for the primary offense. The defendant appealed the sentence, and the Court of Appeals (Kansas) upheld the sentencing court's decision. The defendant appealed the decision.


OVERVIEW: In upholding the defendant's sentence, the court of appeals held that the case of Apprendi v. New Jersey did not apply because the primary facts upon which the defendant's upward departure sentence was based were proven beyond a reasonable doubt by his admissions and pleas of guilty. On appeal, the defendant argued that the imposition of an upward departure sentence was unconstitutional, as the sentencing court based its sentence upon his admissions, not upon facts found beyond a reasonable doubt by a jury. The defendant contended that under Apprendi his guilty plea to the elements of the offense was not an admission that the sentencing factors used to increase his sentence were proved beyond a reasonable doubt. The supreme court's review of the record showed that the sentencing court failed to reveal the precise statute relied upon for its upward departure. The supreme court noted that Kan. Stat. Ann. § 21-4716 (2000), which granted judges the authority to depart from a presumptive sentence, had been found unconstitutional in a prior decision. Therefore, the supreme court reversed the sentence and remanded for resentencing following that prior decision.


OUTCOME: The defendant's sentence was reversed and remanded for resentencing.
